field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe a basic awareness of evolution by genetic mutations and natural selection </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain the Catholic Christian understanding of evolution and how it has changed with scientific evidence </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate God’s role and humanity’s role in evolution according to the Catholic Church </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain the mechanisms behind and current applications of genetic modification </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assess the Church’s understanding of the moral imperative to affect gene mutation in a way that does not compromise our inherent human dignity. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate scientific and theological vocabulary connected to the issues involved.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate an understanding of the Catholic Church’s position on evolution and approach to the natural sciences.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate an awareness of the boundaries of ethical science</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate an understanding of the implications of and moral decisions about modification of humans and nature</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluate arguments about genetic modification of humans from science and the dignity of the human person</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Investigate the role of human involvement in genetic modification and the Catholic church’s position on said development.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Interpret the value of scripture and tradition as applied to genetic modification </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Synthesize and identify the best moral decisions to take regarding genetic modification based on Catholic scripture and tradition </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Intended Audience: Seniors in Science &amp; Religion Elective</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Defining evolution: Day 1 (80 minutes) </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pre-assessment:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>  What does the church teach about God’s role in creation and evolution? (pair-share and class discussion)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Direct Instruction:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain the current understanding of Catholic interpretation of evolution and identify common misconceptions. (</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1fbGg2xAUxcSiYuJuPLNP-UKdryF2f0UpM-cyMVOFqJM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Google Slides</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explore the mechanisms of evolution and how they do not prove God’s existence.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Student Activity:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Students discuss how the elements of evolution allow for a greater understanding of God’s nature.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> </ul> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Direct Instruction:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Present a timeline from the origin of time (Big Bang) to present day. </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Student Activities:</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Students will break into small groups, drawing a timeline focusing on the development of life, simple organisms to complex life.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will investigate how science has arrived at the conclusion that the Universe is 13.8 Billion years old. Students will work in small groups to find an understandable answer that will allow the class to understand the age of the Universe. Students will include when this scientific information was discovered/used.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Investigate how the views of science and religion can be compatible with one another in regards to the creation and evolution of the Universe?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Vocabulary</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Evolution, Inherent dignity of the human person, Free will, Revelation, Co-creators, Bioethics, Ethical discernment, Stewardship, Common Good </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>Exit Ticket:</span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span> What is one way that science and religion are compatible?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>Homework:</span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> What is the role of humans AND God in evolution/creation moving forward? (closing discussion)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Tools for modifying creation: Day 2 (80 minutes) </span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Formative assessment</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: When do humans have the moral authority to intentionally modify creation? (Small group discussion)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Direct instruction</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: How do humans currently modify creation? (</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1fbGg2xAUxcSiYuJuPLNP-UKdryF2f0UpM-cyMVOFqJM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Google Slides</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In this lecture, students will learn about the various methods that have been and are being used to modify creation, including selective breeding of crops/animals, CRISPR, and development of adult stem cells. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Learn the Catholic ethical position on gene editing/engineering</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Vocabulary</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: CRISPR, Genetic modification/engineering, Gene therapy, Regenerative medicine, Biotechnology, DNA, Genome, stem cells</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Group Research Activity</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> (30 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In this activity, students will be provided with a variety of scenarios in which humans have the opportunity to ‘modify creation’. The scenarios include:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Fixing” genome of 22q baby with gene deletion effects</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>“Fixing” genome to get physiological traits desired (strength, eye color, etc)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Production of crops with extra vitamin B in sub-Saharan Africa where vitamin deficiencies are prevalent</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Production of crops that glow in the dark for specialty catering events</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reversion of adult cells to stem cells for treatment of cancer</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reversion of adult cells to stem cells to extend life expectancy for the wealthy who can afford it</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>During this activity, students will choose one scenario and prepare their thoughts about the morality of the modification, the potential benefits/complications, and additional concerns/limitations that need to be addressed; preparation must be supported with text from the previous day as well as additional resources that they find. This activity will prepare students for the small group and class discussions the following day. If there is insufficient time, students can finish their homework.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discussion on Different Creation Modification Scenarios: Day 3 (80 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Group Policy Creation</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: (40 minutes) After individually preparing the previous day on their scenario, all of the students with the same application type (grouped by colors above) will work together to craft a defining guideline for the field of how to determine when this type of modification is morally acceptable.  Students should consider:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How far is too far? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What responsibilities are involved? (What implications need to be considered?)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is there ever a time that it would be morally imperative to modify creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Whole Class Discussion</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: (40 minutes) Once each group has created their policy, they will present their statement to the class and give an explanation at how they arrived at their policy.  Then the class will discuss each of these topics to ultimately answer, “When do humans have the moral authority to intentionally modify creation, and what responsibilities are involved?” </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Summative Assessment: Reflection: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Using the knowledge intended for this lesson, students will write an 8 - 10 sentence reflection that demonstrates their understanding of the scientific, technological, and religious concepts connected to genetic engineering. Students will additionally state their current opinion on the ethical use of gene modification with supportive reasoning.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Pre-assessment:  </span></em></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is the church teaching on God’s role in creation?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Formative assessment:</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Before next class, spend some time thinking about this:  what is the role of humans AND God in evolution/creation moving forward? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Summative assessment: </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Create a policy on the ethical use of genetic modification and communicate your position in a class discussion.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><em><span>Summative assessment: </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Using the knowledge intended for this lesson, students will write an 8 - field--string-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This unit explores end of life issues with an emphasis on understanding how we are called to support those who are dying and how we especially have a duty to protect, pray, and advocate for those who are vulnerable to the evils of capital punishment, suicide, and euthanasia. As students analyze Church documents, learn about the history of end of life legislation, investigate connections of science and medicine, and reflect on their own prior knowledge and attitudes about end of life issues, they will come to integrate this knowledge and synthesize a fuller understanding of the complexities of the passage of the human being from life into death and ultimately Resurrection in Jesus Christ.<br /> <br /> This unit was designed for a three week time frame in a senior honors level bioethics course. Each lesson is designed to be completed in a 45 minute class period, but can easily be adapted to block schedules by allowing students more time for reading, processing, and reflection.<br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will comprehend the dignity of the human person and outline how this dignity entitles each person to “a good death” that includes compassionate end of life care.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will understand the Church’s position on capital punishment and apply these principles to justifying the ethics of executing prisoners.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will explain the science of the effects of lethal injection on the body, terminal and progressive illness, reduced consciousness (coma, persistent vegetative state, and brain death), and the changes the body goes through in the process of dying.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will describe Church teaching on suicide and euthanasia, particularly in morally complex situations that involve progressive disease or reduced consciousness of the patient.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will recall the Church’s attentive nature to the dying person throughout history and at present citing examples such as the Corporal Work of Mercy to Bury the Dead, the Sacrament of Anointing the Sick, and the long tradition of health care for the sick and dying.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>By the end of this unit, students will be able to:</p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>navigate and analyze Church documents, commentary, and websites on end of life care</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>communicate to their family and peers the teachings of the Church on the moral issues of capital punishment, euthanasia, and end of life care</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>apply their knowledge of ordinary and extraordinary means as well as their understanding of the physiology of terminal illness and reduced consciousness (coma, persistent vegetative state, and brain death) to evaluate the ethics of withdrawing life-support in various case studies</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>apply Catholic social teaching in the context of the racial inequalities of capital punishment to advocate for marginalized populations</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>form their consciences about end of life issues</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 1</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Catholicism and the “Good Death”</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introductory rhetorical questions:  Ask students, "What constitutes a 'good death'? Is it peaceful? Surrounded with family? Where does it take place?" </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>On the contrary, what is a “bad death”? Is it violent, vengeful, murderous, lonely? What about a “bad death” specifically makes it bad?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain to students that we will be examining the features of death in bad and good circumstances and what our faith teaches about death</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstration: Show students a $20 and ask its worth. Invite students up to the front to harm the bill in some way (step, draw, etc.) Then ask students if they would still want to keep the bill in its current condition. Explain that the value of the bill doesn’t decrease based on its appearance. Similarly, human life always has an inherent worth and dignity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explore: What is dignity? Ask the students if they can begin to construct a working definition together. Write some thoughts on the side of the whiteboard and revisit this throughout the unit as new insights arise; we will revise our understanding of this word throughout the unit.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Read-Aloud: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="http://www.usccb.org/about/pro-life-activities/respect-life-program/john-paul-ii-dying-with-dignity.cfm"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>John Paul II: Dying with Dignity</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Consider the </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1HuyH98b5yDG7zEYmIUNZep5EZ8mjaBf_v9t_VMa3QXo/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>following questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> from today’s reading and jot down some thoughts to share with the class tomorrow.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 2: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The Dignity of the Human Person</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>At the beginning of class, give each student a green colored pen to add to their notes from yesterday. As the discussion progresses and after the discussion, students will have 10 minutes to record any new insights they have from the reading. This reflection sheet will be collected at the end of class as a formative assessment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Socratic Seminar Style Discussion: Pope John Paul refers to the words from Romans, 14: 7-8 as he is clear about life and death in this world. “ None of us lives to himself , and none of us dies to himself. If we live, we live to the Lord, and if we die, we die to the Lord; so then, whether we live or whether we die, we are the Lord’s “</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>How does the word “ dignity “ arise from these words Pope John Paul uses in his message ?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Pope ends his presentation by saying “Last but not least, respect for the dignity and sanctity of life of patients includes concern for their spiritual needs.“ Reflecting on the suffering that might occur in an end of life issue, what are your thoughts on the physical and spiritual needs of the dying ?</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Debrief: Students will have 10 minutes to write down any new insights they have after the group discussion and they will hand in their sheet at the end of class.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Survey on Google Forms: Examination of Current Attitudes Toward Death (</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/forms/d/1pYwKeFuaKghqJmlXqLmVPeIsw8nXidd6xmjweUBroiY/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Teacher Version</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>, </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSffKcWvfq1k10neH1BW0I6YWyKsTBCUhGmbj3OMMTEW4xE5sw/viewform?usp=sf_link"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Student Version</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 3</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Attitudes Toward Death and Introduction to Capital Punishment</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analysis of Yesterday’s Survey Results: Project the results of the anonymous survey on the board. Ask students: were the majority of students in favor of euthanasia or against it? What about capital punishment? Discuss the results in more depth and ask students if they were surprised at the results.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><a href="https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1w0BBypoWQOypWu3RP27dWLblbAT7ayu53rb-jxLScxI/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lecture</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>: History and Science of Capital Punishment in the US</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Watch: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qsLEODxl35Q"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>TedX Talk “Medical Assistance in Dying: It’s not as easy as it looks” with Dr. Joel Zivot</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> (8:36-14:10 only).</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Compose a paragraph reflection on the following prompts:</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>Currently, the US uses lethal injection for the death penalty becaue it is viewed as the most humane way to die. Based on Dr. Zivot’s analysis of post lethal injection autopsies, is this claim supported or unsupported? Justify your answer by citing specific physiological evidence.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>“There are cases in which executions fail. Albeit they are few and far between, but what do we do in these cases? Is there a moral change in one’s thinking when death does not come quickly?”</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 4</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>:</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span> Capital Punishment Research</span></em></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introductory Video to pique interest from </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xQyYa3DBhNA"><em><span><span><span>Dead Man Walking</span></span></span></em></a> that s</span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>hows an emotional moment between death row inmate Matthew Poncelet with Sr. Helen Prejean. </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>*If your schedule permits, you may consider watching the entire movie with your class over a few days*</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discuss: What is the essential Church teaching being illustrated here? </span></span>What have you heard the Church teach about capital punishment? </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Within Catholicism there are some nuanced teachings on when capital punishment is permissible, and doctrine has unfolded as security of prisons has modernized.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Research: Divide students into two large teams today to research the arguments for and against capital punishment citing evidence from Church documents as well as any other ethical arguments or case studies they feel are relevant. Students will be aware of which side of the argument they will be debating tomorrow in order that they may focus their research on one side in depth. To help organize their thoughts before and during the debate, they should make debate notes using the following </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/11KmX581B_tVBN1sNbx_LjgPDkCqhOdNVPS31YiZi_Tw/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>template</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>In addition to the following resources, which should be printed and distributed, students are strongly encouraged to find more documents on this topic on the </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="http://www.usccb.org/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB website</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> using their Chromebooks. If your school does not have 1:1 devices like Chromebooks or iPads, you may chose to coordinate this as a day in the on-campus library.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><a href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/what-we-do/death-penalty/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Abolish the Death Penalty - Amnesty International</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></p> <p><span><span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=X1eoLxWtIYQ"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Catholic Answers </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></p> <p><span><span><a href="https://cruxnow.com/vatican/2018/08/pope-francis-changes-teaching-on-death-penalty-its-inadmissible/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pope Francis changes teaching on the death penalty</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><a href="https://catholiccitizens.org/views/73332/catholic-defense-capital-punishment/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Catholic Defense of Capital Punishment</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></p> <p><span><span><a href="http://www.usccb.org/issues-and-action/human-life-and-dignity/death-penalty-capital-punishment/statement-on-capital-punishment.cfm"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Bishop’s Statement on Capital Punishment (1980)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></p> <p><span><span><a href="http://usccb.org/issues-and-action/human-life-and-dignity/death-penalty-capital-punishment/upload/penaltyofdeath.pdf"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>A Culture of Life and the Penalty of Death (2005)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Recommended Case Studies: Timothy McVeigh, </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/missouri-holds-nation-s-first-execution-during-coronavirus-pandemic-n1210646"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Walter Barton</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>, Johnny D (“Walter McMillan” from the movie <em>Just Mercy</em>)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Complete the debate template.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 5</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>:</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span> Capital Punishment Debate</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Today students will be debating the arguments for and against capital punishment. They may reference their debate template notes from yesterday.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Complete a one page reflection on the following questions, taking into consideration the points that were brought up in today’s debate. You will be turning in these questions as well as your debate note sheet on Monday.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What are your thoughts on capital punishment after today’s debate? Are you more for the death penalty or against it? Answer honestly, but use information from the debate today to support your points.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Are some victims of capital punishment more deserving than others?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Does God consider perpetrators of capital crimes less worthy of forgiveness than others?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is the death penalty a symptom of a culture of violence or a solution to it?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 6</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>:</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span> Capital Punishment, Mass Incarceration, and Systemic Racism</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introduction: Ask students, "What were some of the most compelling arguments FOR the death penalty from yesterday’s discussion? What were some of the most compelling arguments AGAINST it? Do you think all people on death row deserve to be there? Why or why not?" Explain that t</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>oday we will be considering why there is injustice in our legal system, and tomorrow we will dive deeper into what forensic science can do to minimize wrongful convictions to prevent innocent people from being put on death row.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=u51_pzax4M0">Video</a>: </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>to spark discussion of today’s lesson key question. Students will then consider the following question in a Think-Pair-Share framework:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why are the incarceration rates disproportionately high for people of color? Depending on student insights, teachers may want students to lead this discussion or may want to introduce some more in depth studies and reasons on this phenomenon. A good starting place can be found </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_and_capital_punishment_in_the_United_States"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>here</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=c2tOp7OxyQ8&amp;feature=emb_logo"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Interview with Bryan Stevenson</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. After watching, discuss the following points: How does our identity as a country shape our beliefs about the death penalty? Is inequality an issue that affects everyone or just on those in prison? Remind students that this is the real lawyer behind the movie Just Mercy, which is </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.justmercyfilm.com/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>available for free as of June 2020</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW: Students will complete a journal entry to reflect and process any of the topics over the last few days they wish. They may reflect on what they learned about the intertwining of social justice, mass incarceration and capital punishment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 7:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><em><span> </span></em></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Capital Punishment, Mass Incarceration, and Systemic Racism Continued</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1M6z39xCHgf3dOEq3304DLBvXdAF1hfcDkySWgYdPyMI/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Innocence Project Webquest</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>: Students will examine the Innocence Project website and work in pairs to complete a guided worksheet that explains the causes of wrongful convictions and what can be done to prevent them.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW: Students will be assigned one of four resources to investigate to help prepare for tomorrow’s jigsaw discussion on suicide. If you are unfamiliar with how to conduct a jigsaw discussion, more in depth instructions can be found </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.theteachertoolkit.com/index.php/tool/jigsaw"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>here</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. Then, instruct students to walk to one side of the room (or somewhere slightly off the middle) based on their opinions of suicide in light of yesterday’s reading. You may also decide to put tape on the floor to make these gradients clearer. Read each statement one at a time and give students time to process, reflect, and share their reasoning for where they are standing. An example of this activity can be seen </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L2EPLfCIRHM&amp;list=PLBVNJo7nhINSlFdfuI9l7OANWmZJD--zl&amp;index=18"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>here</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>, and the statements to read are below:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Suicide is always tragic</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Suicide is never morally acceptable</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Suicide should be illegal</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Suicide precludes a soul from entering heaven</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Jigsaw Discussion: As all students have already examined some of their personal beliefs in the first activity today and discussed their articles/video in expert groups the night before, spend the last half of class discussing the </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1CTlKonLyLbA-N3RmDBsUyluSA9wBZxIrVjJ6l_UoJTs/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>following questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> in mixed groups. <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The romanticization of suicide in literature (Romeo and Juliet) and modern media (13 Reasons Why)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How to recognize the symptoms of depression and advocate for your peers and others who may be facing this</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> and caring dialogue about suicide</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> Today students will be given editing access to a Google Sheet with terms they will frequently see in news stories about euthanasia. Each student will choose at least one term to define, cite a source for the definition, illustrate, and explain the significance of. (~20 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>At the end of 20 minutes, the teacher will project the glossary on the board and address the definitions the students provided while sorting out misconceptions as they arise. If any definitions seem obviously incorrect, use it as a teachable moment to analyze the reliability of the source.  This Google Slides presentation can then be saved by the students and referenced as needed throughout the course of the next few days.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1) Watch and read “</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/morning-mix/wp/2014/11/03/how-brittany-maynard-may-change-the-right-to-die-debate-after-death/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>How Brittany Maynard may change the right-to-die debate</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>”</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2) Read </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://licatholic.org/seminarian-to-brittany-maynard-our-lives-are-worth-living-even-with-brain-cancer/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Seminarian with Brain Cancer to Brittany Maynard: Our Lives are Still Worth Living</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3) Reflect: How are Brittany Maynard and Phillip G Johnson similar and different? their experience in the Chapel Activity and which quote spoke most  and 2)  their experience completing the Spiritual and Corporal Works of Mercy of their choice. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 14: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Bury the Dead: Examining Church teaching on burial and treatment of the body after death</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/1JC4MBTFu0McyvxvMV4ZxjfPc5L0KoZv2wX6jAAJifP0/edit?usp=sharing">Lecture</a>*</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: What physiologically happens to a body as it dies? How have cultural practices, religion, and concerns about space shaped our burial customs throughout history? How does the Catholic understanding of the dignity of the human person tie in to how the body is treated when the soul is no longer present in it? Which methods of laying a person to rest are permitted or encouraged by the Church? Which ones are not?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>*Note: Slide 3 contains information about the physiological changes a body goes through after death. It is not particularly graphic, but it is left up to the professional judgement of the teacher, their knowledge of their students, and the context of the class (for example, this information would be routine in Forensics, but perhaps atypical in traditional Apologetics) to decide if they want to show the first part of the Human Burial video on Slide 3 or jump directly to the second half on Slide 4*</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Research Activity: Students will be provided with a printed set of sources on Catholic burial customs (see slides above) and work in teams of 4 or 5 to skim the sources and sill out the summary sheet on </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1dgPyOaY784o12HZuPKR4YHtrdaP93SLbPbOORYnbAp8/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Treatment of the Body After Death</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discussion: see slides above</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>HW: Work on template for </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1V8Pxm250Xm7T0OEBFRPtlW-JNzBqL6ab7JKjdxsmjrA/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>End of Life Narrative</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day 15:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span> Writing End of Life Narratives</span></em></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will take out the template for the end of unit project they filled out yesterday and spend the class period continuing to</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> construct a story in which a person faces one of the end of life issues covered in the unit (capital punishment, suicide, euthanasia, hospice, burial customs)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>They will also compose an answer key on a separate document which explains if the conclusion of the story was morally acceptable or morally problematic, in light of Catholic teaching.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Day 16: </strong><em>Evaluating End of Life Narratives</em></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Printed copies of end of life narratives and answer keys will be due today. Student authors will be evaluated on the detail of their narrative, as well as the reasoning and accuracy of the claims made in the answer key.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Additionally, today each student will receive another student’s story (without the answer key) and be charged with creating their own answer key  to justify whether or not the story demonstrated a conclusion that was morally acceptable or problematic. They may use any printed articles or  notes they wish, and they will submit their answer at the end of class as a summative assessment of the unit.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>Formative assessments are embedded in the daily lesson plans, a take home quiz is assigned on Day 9, and a summative unit assessment can be found on Days 15 and 16. Please refer to the Methods Section for assessments.</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB Standards</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>VI. Life in Jesus Christ, II. God Has Taught Us How to Live a New Life in Christ </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>5) Fifth Commandment: You shall not kill. a) Respect human life in all its stages and situations (CCC, nos. 2258- 2262). b) Legitimate self-defense and the death penalty (CCC, nos. 2263-2267). c) Principles regarding health, science, bodily integrity (CCC, nos. 2292- 2301). d) Sins against the Fifth Commandment: murder; suicide; abortion; euthanasia; embryonic stem cell research; abuse of alcohol, drugs, food, or tobacco; abuse of the body (CCC, nos. 364, 2268-2283, 2290-2291).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>V. Sacraments as Privileged Encounters with Jesus Christ, III. Sacraments of Healing </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>B. Anointing of the Sick: the sacrament which gives spiritual healing and strength to a person seriously ill and sometimes also physical recovery (CCC, nos. 1499-1513). 1. Understanding the sacrament. a. Scriptural basis: Jas 5:14-15 (CCC, no. 1510). b. Historical development (CCC, no. 1512). c. Theology. 1) Illness (CCC, nos. 1500-1502). 2) Christ the Physician (CCC, no. 1503). 3) Faith and healing (CCC, no. 1504). 4) Christ’s suffering (CCC, no. 1505). 5) Disciples carry cross (CCC, no. 1506). 6) Holy Spirit’s gift of healing (CCC, no. 1509). 7) Christ institutes sacrament of the sick (CCC, nos. 1500-1513).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>II. Who Is Jesus Christ?, V. Challenges, C. How can people say that God is good if suffering and evil are present in the world?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. The Passion and Death of Jesus can help us to see beyond suffering and remind us that God is present with us in our suffering, pain, and death; our own personal suffering when united to Jesus’ suffering becomes redemptive for ourselves and others (CCC, no. 1851).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>V. Sacraments as Privileged Encounters with Jesus Christ, V. Challenges to Worship and Sacraments </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. The Sacrament of the Anointing of the Sick can have different effects. Sometimes Christ does bring about physical healing through that sacrament. Other times, the healing is spiritual in that it helps the person to be better prepared for death, to be at peace, and to be eager to be with the Lord.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>NGSS Standards</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p><a href="http://www.nap.edu/openbook.php?record_id=13165&amp;page=143"><span><span><span><span><span><span>LS1.A: Structure and Function</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <ul> <li> <p><a href="http://www.nap.edu/openbook.php?record_id=13165&amp;page=143"><span><span><span><span><span><span>Systems of specialized cells within organisms help them perform the essential functions of life. (HS-LS1-1)</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> </li> <li> <p><a href="http://www.nap.edu/openbook.php?record_id=13165&amp;page=143"><span><span><span><span><span><span>Multicellular organisms have a hierarchical structural organization, in which any one system is made up of numerous parts and is itself a component of the next level. (HS-LS1-2)</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> </li> <li> <p><a href="http://www.nap.edu/openbook.php?record_id=13165&amp;page=143"><span><span><span><span><span><span>Feedback mechanisms maintain a living system’s internal conditions within certain limits and mediate behaviors, allowing it to remain alive and functional even as external conditions change within some range. Feedback mechanisms can encourage (through positive feedback) or discourage (negative feedback) what is going on inside the living system. (HS-LS1-3)</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> </li> </ul> <p> </p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">The Church’s teachings on end-of-life issues are subtle and yet crucial for human happiness. What exactly is euthanasia? How could the Church’s teachings about human dignity lead patients to experience a peaceful death, even in the face of great suffering? This lesson helps students clarify misunderstandings about the Church’s teachings on end-of-life issues by exploring and applying the moral principles underlying those teachings and by reflecting on the power of redemptive suffering in their own lives and in the lives of others.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>There are biological and genetic characteristics of humans that are shared with other animal species.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Unlike other mammals, the human person is a unity of body and rational soul.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Being near death in no way invalidates the fact of one’s personhood and dignity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Church is committed to offering palliative care to those who are near death.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Church teaches that euthanasia is a grave offense against the dignity of the human person and a sin against the Fifth Commandment.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The Church’s teachings on end-of-life care promote redemptive suffering as a means to eternal beatitude (or happiness).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' -->
