'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Identify biological similarities shared between humans and other mammals.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summarize St. Thomas’s understanding of the human soul and explain how the human soul sets humans apart from other mammals.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>State and describe principles of moral theology that pertain to end-of-life issues.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Synthesize, disseminate, and apply Church teachings to real-life end-of-life situations.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analyze a peer’s short story and explain how it incarnates particular Church teachings about end-of-life issues.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong>A Note about the Lesson's Title</strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Consider <em>not</em> showing students the title of the lesson plan at the beginning of the lesson. The lesson is meant to create space for students to discover on their own the Church's teachings on the morality of different end-of-life situations. Thus, the wording “Reclaiming True Dignity from the Euthanasia Movement” might make students feel like they are being told what to think before the lesson even starts.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><strong>Day One (45 minutes)</strong></p> <ul> <li><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/e/2PACX-1vQLyXLtmZH4gopEzMECVF2qf06CQgPKD2EogG45WnAmhE_LloevZegX0aeuMsRP8D-TArf8l8yIz81r/pub"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Opening Activity</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. Lead students through a series of activities that will be used for a discussion to address common misconceptions of what it means to be alive.  (</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1MkS264I6_CMgtZDYXSGqrf1gx_R8sBct1EaGNkgy1Ac/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Opening Activity Rationale</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><a href="http://scienceforseminaries.org/resource/to-be-human/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science for Seminaries Video</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. Watch a brief, nine-minute video on the evolutionary and genetic similarities humans share with other animals.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Choose 2 or 3 of the questions in </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.scienceforseminaries.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/Study-Guide-To-Be-Human.pdf"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>this document</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> to have students write a brief response to and then lead a class discussion on the questions.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Show <a href="https://aquinas101.thomisticinstitute.org/body-and-soul">this video</a> about the unity of body and soul. Students complete the corresponding <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1AuYohQHogrMAib869c7WoK-v3vtqaoM_4bI8kpr2zYs/edit">worksheet</a>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Exit Ticket.</span></span> On a half-sheet of paper, each student writes: (1) o<span><span><span><span><span><span>ne sentence about what he learned today; (2) o<span><span><span><span><span><span>ne sentence about what he still finds confusing from today; (3) o</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>ne sentence about what more he wants to know about the learning from today.</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1q79qqnOGPiWQm8lRvqLN_mtGV02THw15sYV4njJMUG0/edit?usp=sharing">Homework</a>. Create a very short story.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Day Two (70 minutes)</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1X17fN3ChX1k-1qavxF5ZLo9VVKDRsfvrpbMAySEKjMM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pre-Assessment</span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>: How Much Do You Know about the Church’s Teachings on Euthanasia?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Story Time. After the above activity, the teacher should separate students into three groups. One group should consist of all students who wrote a story describing situation (i) for Day One’s homework; a second group should consist of all students who wrote a story describing situation (ii); and a third group should consist of all students who wrote a story describing situation (iii). (Hopefully, each group will have at least a handful of students in it.) Then, the teacher will compose small groups of three to five students each by selecting one or more students from each large group to join each small group. (This guarantees students in the small group will read a variety of stories.) Once in small groups, students will arrange their desks in a circle and each student will read aloud his or her story. If students have also posted their stories on a discussion board, after groups have finished listening to the stories, students may use their electronic devices to access the discussion board and read some of the other stories.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discussion. The teacher will facilitate a whole-class discussion about the stories by asking students some of the </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1kVlIUizuclgwtsC8Sv_sfv5XNcppUWHvPMUMKzypjIM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>discussion questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. It is very possible that the class will need more time for the discussion. It could definitely overflow into day three while still leaving enough time for that day’s Socratic seminar.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Homework. Read and annotate Trent Horn’s article </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://drive.google.com/open?id=1bj6D27iwEDAhqiVyV1DNWDaLbvHOlQo97LEUOgxsTSg"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>On the So-Called ‘Choice in Dying’</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. Annotations should include underlining or highlighting, writing short summary notes, questions, or comments in the margins, and identifying unfamiliar words and writing their definitions nearby. Comments may include personal reactions to the text, connections to learning from other classes, or connections to film, literature, or music.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Day Three (70 minutes)</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Homework Check. If time permits at the beginning of class, the teacher should check to see if the students have thoroughly completed their annotations.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Socratic Seminar. The teacher facilitates a Socratic seminar wherein the students discuss the Horn article. The main purpose of the article is to show the impoverishment of the individualist attitude of “my death, my choice.” The instructor may wish to ask some of these </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1JnCWgdRcjvVfeLWgYndEFlGfHUvfCxdX2qGD5BgvK-A/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>questions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> to start and guide the discussion. (Of course, the nature of the article may be enough to incite some vigorous debate among the students. That’s fine; but students should be encouraged to cite evidence to support whatever claims they make.)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Homework.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <span><span><span><span><span><span>Students must complete the </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Pm7y6CMII0GaQnWzl8dqno5dhHXWa5RHm9rmMA6F-kk/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Socratic seminar closure form</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> for tomorrow.</span></span></span></span></span></span> (<span><span><span><span><span><span>If the teacher wanted to give additional homework, he could assign each student a reading (see Day Four, Step One) to do at home. Then, on Day Four, students can begin midway through Step Two by forming their expert groups and discussing the readings.)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><strong>Day Four (45 minutes)</strong></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Jigsaw Activity. Students will explore the moral principles governing the Church's teachings on end-of-life issues. Student readings are <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1OXGIBzA99jw_fo1gn0oKa7WagA5tXrRPZdM1wNwBYNc/edit">here</a>; teacher instructions are <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1pAowXxFi0vfpQZ9lVraVq2PHlR-CXQ12zJFur-AAfKw/edit?usp=sharing">here</a>; and further information about how a jigsaw works is <a href="https://itali.uq.edu.au/files/3077/Resources-teaching-methods-jigsawtechnique.pdf">here</a>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Day Five (45 minutes)</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Case Study. Some students will read aloud the <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1r5s_6-UWa9p3TMHHtDjRXy-CQzeIM94Oc8jC7jtsiUQ/edit">case study about Mary Hartney's death</a>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discussion and Application of Moral Principles. Teacher instructions are <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1CTH900nrix3BYFQZEKfwgaFO3betdhEfycxh035-toY/edit?usp=sharing">here</a>.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><strong>Day Six (70 minutes)</strong></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1sk2ep79bbMwFsVD9oM34Wh_8apbCSxHAPBr6FG8_RQU/edit?usp=sharing">Practice Applying Moral Principles</a>. In this activity, students will revisit the short stories their peers wrote at the beginning of the lesson in order to discern which situations the Church deems morally permissible and which situations are morally problematic.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Guest Speaker Testimony about Redemptive Suffering. If possible, the teacher could invite to the classroom a Christian who has experienced great suffering who would be willing to offer a testimony about that suffering and how his Christian faith helped him to find the redemptive elements in it. While it would be of particular relevance to the unit if the suffering were related to end-of-life issues, it could also have occurred for other reasons. A testimony like this would help students see how suffering is not meaningless. Similarly, the suffering one may endure at the end of his life can be shot through with meaning (and can have positive effects, some of which Father Robert Spitzer mentions </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="http://www.euthanasia.com/spitzer.html"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>here</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>; others of which students encountered in various readings throughout the unit).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Prayerful Reflection. Bring students to the chapel. Display a crucifix in a prominent area. Invite students to meditate on Christ’s suffering on the cross. Perhaps select a few students to read some key passages from the Gospel that highlight Christ’s sufferings. A few students could also compose and read petitions asking that God will intercede to help those who are suffering understand how it can be redemptive. The teacher may also wish to play a song that discusses consolation in the face of suffering (such as Laura Story’s </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Cd6J6Wgnv4M"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Blessings</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> or Kristene Dimarco’s </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OjxwryxSrIY"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>I Am No Victim</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>). The teacher could also give students </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1eqxsQl2uGxqx7qEGW8Xz9rRCJprRpr_7DitB9LXriMA/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>short excerpts from John-Paul II’s encyclical </span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span><span><span>Salvifici Doloris</span></span></span></em></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> and invite them to reflect on the meaning of those excerpts for their own lives.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Day Seven (70 minutes)</strong> (The instructor may wish to denote more than merely one day to this activity.)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will select two elements of Catholic teaching about euthanasia or end-of-life care that they learned from this lesson, and use those elements to do a <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1VRpdrSpjKERkbXe5XLovbBLalTqeA_F9nU5ZOFkWblY/edit?usp=sharing">creative project</a>. [Note: The teacher may wish to refrain from telling the students about Part Four of the project until students have finished Part Three. The teacher may also wish to share the <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1QzxEXyOwaMxq5jbuyYv3vfTsaxjldSvbVsgR4Y0Atls/edit?usp=sharing">project rubric</a> with students when the project is first introduced.]</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Last Day (45 minutes)</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In-Class Essay. </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1LJaX9JBP5ZrPPqc_bU0JFDHsAeCBZJ_0HD-IUi5y54o/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>This document</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> contains two prompts for an in-class essay. Students will select one prompt and spend forty-five minutes writing a four- or five-paragraph essay addressing the prompt. These <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1qHRzbhdK9CLxVY554TSFsC86zrKupdwMJXcxToqA-bk/edit?usp=sharing">rubrics</a> will aid the teacher in grading the finished product.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Closing Discussion. Alternatively, teachers may choose one prompt and require all students to write an essay addressing that prompt. Then, they could use the other prompt for a closing discussion during a different 45-minute class period.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pre-assessments: Teacher-led discussion following the opening activity; <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1X17fN3ChX1k-1qavxF5ZLo9VVKDRsfvrpbMAySEKjMM/edit?usp=sharing">“How Much Do You Know about the Church’s Teachings on Euthanasia?”</a></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Formative assessments: Class discussions; exit tickets; a check of students’ annotations; <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Pm7y6CMII0GaQnWzl8dqno5dhHXWa5RHm9rmMA6F-kk/edit">Socratic seminar closure form</a>; jigsaw</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Reflective Assessment: Reflection on </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Salvifici Doloris</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> and redemptive suffering</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Summative Assessments: Create a short story about an end-of-life issue that incarnates Catholic moral principles; <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1LJaX9JBP5ZrPPqc_bU0JFDHsAeCBZJ_0HD-IUi5y54o/edit">in-class essay</a> with <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1qHRzbhdK9CLxVY554TSFsC86zrKupdwMJXcxToqA-bk/edit?usp=sharing">rubric</a></span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>HS-LS4-1 </span></span>Communicate scientific information that common ancestry and biological evolution are supported by multiple lines of empirical evidence.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Theology</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB Framework Course VI. Life in Jesus Christ</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I.A.2.a God created us in his image and likeness; the dignity of the human person.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I.B.3 What it means to be a follower of Christ.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>II.B.5.d Sins against the Fifth Commandment: murder; suicide; abortion; euthanasia;. . . abuse . . . of the body.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>V.A.3 In reality, sinful actions diminish freedom; moral acts increase it.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>V.C.1 The Church has the responsibility to teach everyone as persuasively as possible about what God has revealed about how people should live, act, and treat each other; fulfilling this responsibility is not the same as the Church imposing her own view on others . . . The Church promotes the universal moral law and the common good, not her own ecclesiastical disciplines.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from Rationale</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p><a href="http://scienceforseminaries.org/resource/to-be-human/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science for video</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>  </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://aquinas101.thomisticinstitute.org/body-and-soul"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Body and Soul</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p><a href="https://drive.google.com/open?id=1AuYohQHogrMAib869c7WoK-v3vtqaoM_4bI8kpr2zYs"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Body and Soul Viewing Guide Worksheet</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1q79qqnOGPiWQm8lRvqLN_mtGV02THw15sYV4njJMUG0/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day One Homework Instructions</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Day Two</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1X17fN3ChX1k-1qavxF5ZLo9VVKDRsfvrpbMAySEKjMM/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pre-Assessment</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> field--string-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This two part lesson will begin by considering how Catholic Social Teaching on Human Dignity should guide the development and proliferation of CRISPR technology. As an application of this, students will consider the difference between gene therapy and gene enhancement. In the second part of the lesson, students will research a particular example of a gene-based therapy that has been (or will be) used therapeutically. During the course of their work, students will also be called to address the economic, social, and moral issues that are involved with the treatment. Students will engage in critical thinking about the need for and value of ethical considerations in the exploration and experimentation of gene therapy applications.<br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>1. <span><span><span><span><span>Articulate the Catholic Concept of the Dignity of the Human Person.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>2. <span><span><span><span><span>Define the term eugenics and justify how it is not permissible given the Catholic understanding of the Dignity of the Human Person.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>3. Explain how the CRISPR method of gene therapy works to target and modify genetic material.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>4. Consider all possible implications (ex. economic, moral, etc...) of a gene-based therapy being used as a medical intervention for a disease. </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>1. <span><span><span><span><span>Evaluate the difference between genetic therapy and genetic enhancement.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>2. <span><span><span><span><span>Argue how the theory/practice of eugenics violates the dignity of the human person.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>3. Analyze the social and economic consequences (good or bad) of genetic therapies for a particular condition or disease.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>4. Critique the necessity for and value of ethical considerations when developing genetic therapy.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>5. <span><span><span><span><span>Articulate the difference between the concepts of the secular bioethics technology imperative (because science is able to do it, science should do it) and the more religious bioethical imperative of considering just because science is able to do it, should we do it? “Can” does not equal “should”.</span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Proposed lesson plan:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Multi-lesson: 2-4 lessons, 60 minutes each.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson One (Introduce the students to Catholic Social Teaching on Human Dignity, Eugenics, CRISPR technology and Genetic Therapy vs. Genetic Enhancement. This may take 1-2 class sessions):</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>1. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Prayer: Lord, you created the heavens, the earth, and all living things.  Help us to see the beauty and order in your creation, and to receive the gifts you have given us to realize our full potential and in so doing, return the love you have given to us. Amen.</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>2. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Learning objectives - by the end of the lesson, students will be able to:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe the Catholic Social Teaching on the Dignity of the Human Person</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Define the term eugenics</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain how the CRISPR method of gene therapy works to target and modify genetic material</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluate the difference between genetic therapy and genetic enhancement</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why are these learning objectives important? (I pose this question to the students and invite them to answer, to provide an opportunity for safe sharing and to encourage participation - no wrong answers!)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Catholic Social Teaching on the Dignity of the Human Person.  For this part, refer to Cardinal Bernardin’s document, “The Seamless Garment”. Link to “The Seamless Garment”: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1DndG_AsMzxNZhcMhiX7ZT6j1oK2lBkyr1aMJCQ-f9AU/edit?usp=sharing"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://docs.google.com/document/d/1DndG_AsMzxNZhcMhiX7ZT6j1oK2lBkyr1aMJCQ-f9AU/edit?usp=sharing</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>  This document includes the following:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>God is the author of all life</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Life is a gift</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>There is no unanimous scientific agreement on when life begins</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Cardinal Bernardin quotes the Catechism of the Catholic Church: all life is sacred “from the first moment of existence” (Catechism, 2270)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Social ethical issues such as human rights (which could include medical treatment and therapy) must show moral consistency and from the above “first moment of existence”, “a human being must be recognized as having the rights of a person” (Catechism, 2270)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. What is eugenics? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>The following are resources for eugenics from which the bullet points below are drawn: <strong>p</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>odcast </span></span></strong><span><span>on History of Eugenics (</span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://15minutehistory.org/podcast/episode-18-eugenics/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://15minutehistory.org/podcast/episode-18-eugenics</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>), <strong>article </strong>on Eugenics in America (</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1DhZodancK9pfzbdQSOkEDZlkQY-Cno1-/view">https://drive.google.com/file/d/1DhZodancK9pfzbdQSOkEDZlkQY-Cno1-/view</a>), and an <strong>article</strong> on Abortion and Eugenics written by Justice Thomas (</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.firstthings.com/web-exclusives/2019/05/abortion-and-eugenics">https://www.firstthings.com/web-exclusives/2019/05/abortion-and-eugenics</a>).</p> <ul> <li> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>The term comes from the Greek, meaning “good breeding”.  The birth of the eugenics movement is linked to British scientist, Sir Francis Galton.  Galton first coined the term <em>eugenics</em> in 1883. He sought to replace Natural Selection (Galton was a distant relative of Charles Darwin) with other means that were more effective at ensuring the proliferation of certain traits. Galton was primarily interested in intelligence. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </li> <li> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>The practice of eugenics can refer to selecting against so-called undesirable traits OR actively selecting for individuals with desirable traits. It is important to understand that these 'traits' certainly included phenotypes but also encompassed categories of gender, economic status and race.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </li> <li> <p>Common eugenic actions<span><span><span><span><span><span> included: compulsory sterilization, medical experimentation, and abortion. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </li> <li> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Can anyone give an example of eugenics in history? (solicit responses first before this next step). </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </li> <li> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>We often associate eugenics with Hitler and the medical experimentation that was done in Nazi Germany frequently in the concentration camps. However, there were surprising policies and practices in the U.S. even before Hitler rose to power. Hitler actually borrowed eugenic policies from the U.S., such as the ban on interracial marriage and compulsory sterilization.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </li> <li> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>There were supporters of eugenics that might surprise you - Theodore Roosevelt, Alexander Graham Bell, and John D. Rockefeller, Jr.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lots of eugenic policy was aimed at women, people of color, the poor, and the institutionalized. In the U.S. by the 1930’s, 27 states had compulsory involuntary sterilization.  California had the highest number of sterilized individuals. Most states kept compulsory sterilization on the books and practiced it until the 1970’s.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>5. What is CRISPR? </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>(Note that there is embedded assessment when I poll the students about some of the details that were in the video after watching it).</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> A brief animated video here will explain what it is and its process.  Link to YouTube video “What is Gene Editing and How Does It Work?” (4:22): </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XPDb8tqgfjY"><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XPDb8tqgfjY</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></a></p> <ul> <li>BASIC CONCEPT behind CRISPR - it <span><span><span><span><span><span>can be likened to the following analogy: let’s say you have a set of 10 volumes of Encyclopedias.  The CRISPR process can change in Volume 4, page 39, paragraph 9, line 4, the letter “d” to the letter “c”.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Poll students. What were some of the benefits indicated in the video? (possible answers: cure a disease, potential for fixing gene mutations that predispose people to certain cancers, enable new therapies for HIV, edit genes that cause hereditary diseases, etc...)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Poll students. What are some of the downsides the video identified of gene editing? (possible answers: editing in human embryos for characteristics that have non-therapeutic reasons, like designer babies, potential to affect not only the affected person but their descendants as well, etc...)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Poll students. What are some ethical and societal concerns to consider that the video included? (possible answers: regulating CRISPR's applications, misuse for eugenic ends, etc..) </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>*DEPENDING ON THE TIME, IT MAY BE ADVISABLE TO STOP THE LESSON HERE AND PICK UP AT STEP 6 FOR THE NEXT CLASS PERIOD.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>**IF YOU CHOOSE TO STOP, CONSIDER CLOSING BY DOING A KNOWLEDGE CHECK ASKING STUDENTS TO DESCRIBE: (a) THE CATHOLIC SOCIAL TEACHING ON THE DIGNITY OF THE HUMAN PERSON AND HOW THIS RENDERS THE PRACTICE OF EUGENICS ILLICIT, and (b) HOW CRISPR, WHEN MISS APPLIED LINKS TO (a).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>***THIS KNOWLEDGE CHECK CAN BE DONE ORALLY (whole class) or THROUGH A JOURNAL ENTRY or A HOMEWORK REFLECTION. In the next class, this knowledge check will form the basis for an activity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>*********************************************************</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>LESSON ONE, PART TWO:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p>6. <span><span><span><span><span><span>The CRISPR technology can be used for genome (genetic material) therapy and enhancement. Fr. Nicanor Pier Giorgio Austriaco, a Dominican priest, is a professor of biology and theology at Providence College in Rhode Island, has written an article that describes the distinction between genetic therapy vs. genetic enhancement.  He argues the moral case for what he deems “Therapeutic Enhancement”.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>ARTICLE LINK: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span>Rev. Nicanor Pier Giorgio Austracio, OP “Healthier than Healthy: The Moral Case for Therapeutic Enhancement” (2017 The National Catholic Bioethics Center)  </span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1WCy5QR8-7OmgUuqGvObZM7LDMY3VVDm4/view"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://drive.google.com/file/d/1WCy5QR8-7OmgUuqGvObZM7LDMY3VVDm4/view</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>     </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>SUPPORTING INFORMATION: Congregation for the Doctrine Of The Faith encyclical, </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Dignitas Personae</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>, from which Austriaco quotes: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span>“Instruction Dignitas Personae On Certain Bioethical Questions”</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="http://www.vatican.va/roman_curia/congregations/cfaith/documents/rc_con_cfaith_doc_20081208_dignitas-personae_en.html"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>http://www.vatican.va/roman_curia/congregations/cfaith/documents/rc_con_cfaith_doc_20081208_dignitas-personae_en.html</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Sickle-cell anemia (CSA)- an inherited disorder that results in patients not having enough healthy red blood cells to transport oxygen through their bodies.  The cases are increasing, and one study projects that SCA cases will increase from over 305,000 in 2010 to over 404,000 by 2050.  UC Berkeley and UC San Francisco published a joint paper describing how they used the CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing system to correct the gene mutation that causes SCA in blood stem cells from affected patients.  They transplanted the genetically engineered stem cells into mice and they survived for an extended time.  This suggests the use of CRISPR to possibly cure or eradicate SCA in the near future.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Fr. Austriaco addresses the significant role in many contemporary ethical discussions about gene editing as making the important distinction between therapy and enhancement. He defines genetic therapies as those that restore the patient to a normal state or counter damage caused by pathology or anomaly.  He defines genetic enhancements as those that improve or strengthen the gene pool beyond the species norm.  He uses an example where therapy can also enhance and therefore it blurs the distinction between therapy and enhancement.  He argues for the replacement of the distinction between therapy and non-therapy, acknowledging that some therapies are enhancements.  He cautions that we should also deploy the benefits/burdens distinction (do the benefits of the therapy outweigh any risks?)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Fr. Austriaco quotes from the Congregation For The Doctrine Of The Faith in their encyclical </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Dignitatis personae</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> how they deem gene therapy.  The document is linked above.  The document says: “Procedures used on somatic cells for strictly therapeutic purposes are in principle morally licit” (Paragraphs 26-27).  Somatic cells are cells other than cells involved in reproduction.  Morally licit means morally okay.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Fr. Austriaco uses the example of treatment of high cholesterol to argue for gene editing that makes patients “healthier than healthy” to be allowed.  With LDL (“bad” cholesterol), if it’s too high, it can lead to cardiovascular disease.  He argues that many cardiologists will say that not only is lowering LDL with medication good within the acceptable range, but that treating it with medication to lower it even further, maybe even lower than the “normal” range, could be a good thing.  He argues that this could be considered enhancement, because lowering it even further to below the normal range would be more than just restoring the patient to a normal state (the normal range) but would be improving beyond the species norm, which would be considered enhancement.  He argues that therapeutic enhancement would be a better term to use to describe what we’re already doing pharmacologically (with medication).</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>He says that if we do this already, and if we consider genetic alterations with technology such as CRISPR to introduce lipid-lowering mutations, then we can argue that they are good, beneficial, and justifiable. This would does not contradict the guidance in Dignitas Personae document which warns against, namely, leading to “dissatisfaction or even rejection of the value of the human being”, nor would it promote “a eugenic mentality and would lead to indirect social stigma with regard to people who lack certain qualities” (paragraphs 26-27).  He uses immunizations as well as an example of enhancement that would not violate these principles.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Importantly, he includes that all efforts should be made to ensure this technology’s or procedure’s interventions accessibility to all, not “limited to the rich and elite, so that the poor and marginalized can benefit”. Also, it is important to consider the benefits and risks of any genetic therapy.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>7. Knowledge check based on learning objectives (this is an embedded assessment, refer to assessment section below for more details):</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to describe Catholic Social Teaching on the Dignity of the Human Person while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to define eugenics while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to explain how the CRISPR technology works while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to differentiate between genetic therapy and genetic enhancement while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>8. Our next lesson will look at specific applications of genetic therapy and any ethical issues that it might entail.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>____________________________________</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Two (which will delve into a particular example of how genome therapy can apply to conditions or diseases and address ethical and moral issues; it may take up two or three class sessions):</span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p>1. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Prayer: Johannes Kepler, a 16th century German astronomer, mathematician, astrologer, best known for his laws of planetary motion, wrote: “I thank thee, Lord God our Creator, that thou allowest me to see the beauty in thy work of creation”.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>2. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Learning objectives - by the end of this lesson, students will be able to:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe a medical condition or disease, its symptoms, and how it is transmitted</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analyze the moral, social, and economical consequences of genetic therapy/enhancement for a particular condition or disease</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why are these learning objectives important? (I pose this question to the students and invite them to answer, to provide an opportunity for safe sharing and to encourage participation - no wrong answers!)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Students will be broken into groups of 3-5 and research a medical condition or disease, its symptoms, and how the condition is transmitted (by either anomaly, defective/problematic gene or DNA sequence, inheritance pattern). Use specific conditions like Down Syndrome, genetic blindness, genetic deafness, Autism Spectrum Disorder.  These all have genetic or have genetic potential causes and might spark more debate.  Use the following reputable websites to gather your information: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://www.nih.gov/"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://www.nih.gov/</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><strong><span><span>   </span></span></strong></span></span></span><a href="https://www.mayoclinic.org/"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://www.mayoclinic.org/</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><strong><span><span>   </span></span></strong></span></span></span><a href="https://www.medlineplus.gov/"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://www.medlineplus.gov/</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. Students create a slideshow with their findings, using words and if applicable, diagrams and pictures as well.  Students should include a description of CRISPR technology for their specific condition/disease. Has there already been work done in this area?  Link to rubric for slideshow: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/11o_pUIVVvwFzLpGrec8hVovN9XsGmw5evLYPVhk-A-o/edit"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://docs.google.com/document/d/11o_pUIVVvwFzLpGrec8hVovN9XsGmw5evLYPVhk-A-o/edit</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p> <p>5. <span><span><span><strong><span><span>Embedded assessment: As groups are working on their research, check in with groups to review their work, gauging their depth of thought and comprehension.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>6. Therapeutic genome editing can be done in one of three ways: by introducing the CRISPR-Cas9 system directly into the adult human patient to correct a genetic defect; edit the genomes of patient-derived stem or progenitor cells to correct their genetic deficiency then be reintroduced to the patient; introduce the CRISPR-Cas9 system into developing human embryos, which in theory would correct the genome in all cells of the organism including reproductive cells. Austriaco, in his document, “Genome Editing with CRISPR”, addresses this.  He argues for the first two, but indicates that the last is morally illicit (not morally okay per Catholic Church teaching). Link to Austriaco’s document:  </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1FZ5ScV2fv8vkHJ-w3ogGlffvGuXAGVy4/view"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://drive.google.com/file/d/1FZ5ScV2fv8vkHJ-w3ogGlffvGuXAGVy4/view</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a></p> <p>7. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Provide groups enough time to complete their slideshow.  Groups will be presenting their slideshow next class (time permitting, or if they need more time, the class after that).  If there is not enough time left in this class for this, provide time next class for completion of slideshow and possible sharing, time permitting. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>*************************************************************</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>TIME OUT HERE FOR GROUPS TO RESEARCH AND COMPLETE THEIR SLIDESHOWS.  IT MAY BE NECESSARY TO PROVIDE NOT ONLY THE REST OF THIS CLASS, BUT ALSO NEXT CLASS FOR COMPLETION OF SLIDESHOW.  WHEN COMPLETED, EACH GROUP CAN PRESENT.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>**************************************************************</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>LESSON TWO PART TWO Cont.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p>8. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Each group presents their slideshow on their researched genetic condition. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>9. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Panel discussion time. One student from each of the research groups will make up the panel, as well as a volunteer student as the moderator (panel discussion host), who will ask questions below and will moderate responses from the panel members  and comments from the class.  From our discussion in our previous lessons, based on Catholic Social Teaching on the Dignity of the Human Person, Eugenics, and the description of genetic therapy, we can discuss the following questions: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Should CRISPR technology be done?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Who decides?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Who pays for it? (government health care, private health care, out of pocket?)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What are some ethical concerns specific to the application of CRISPR? These concerns SHOULD include the therapy vs modification concern, upholding the dignity of the human person, etc... but must also include the dangers of CRISPR being used to select against certain races, gender, mental capacities, etc... ALL of these concerns point to students needing to be aware that, ethically, this technology must be considered carefully lest it be used in a eugenic fashion.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What about the dignity of the INDIVIDUAL person receiving the gene therapy? (e.g., what if Helen Keller had had gene therapy or her teacher Annie Sullivan?  What might have happened? Should we assume that it’s “better to be sighted” or “better to be hearing”? Why?)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Given a given group's research, did their view on the application of CRISPR change at all given the notable people with their researched condition?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What if your parents were pregnant with a fetus with your researched condition?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Resources for this lesson include: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Devan Stahl, “Moral Evaluations of Genetic Technologies: The Need for Catholic Social Doctrine” (2015 The National Catholic Bioethics Center)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/18JGZde49MsfLJz3oqQg3Xx9XLEnrwaYn/view"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://drive.google.com/file/d/18JGZde49MsfLJz3oqQg3Xx9XLEnrwaYn/view</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><strong><span><span>    Quotes from above document:  P. 485 Reverence for the person; P. 489 Universal access, rich/poor gap.  </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Also, </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>From Ethics &amp; Medics A Commentary of The National Catholic Bioethics Center on Health Care and the Life Sciences, March 2016 Volume 41, Number 3.  Article linked below is “Genome Editing with CRISPR” by Rev. Nicanor Pier Giorgio Austriaco, OP</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1FZ5ScV2fv8vkHJ-w3ogGlffvGuXAGVy4/view"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://drive.google.com/file/d/1FZ5ScV2fv8vkHJ-w3ogGlffvGuXAGVy4/view</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a></p> <p>10. <span><span><span><strong><span><span>Knowledge check based on learning objectives (this is an embedded assessment, refer to assessment section below for more details):</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to describe how the theory/practice of eugenics violates the dignity of the human person while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask students to share their opinion on the necessity for ethical considerations (take poll on how many think it’s necessary and write that number of students on the board). Then, ask students to share their opinion of the value of ethical considerations or administration over scientific exploration and experimentation while I write them on the whiteboard.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Have students share their thoughts on the difference between the concepts of the secular bioethics technology imperative (because science is able to do it, science should do it) and the more religious bioethical imperative of considering just because science is able to do it, should we do it?  “Can” does </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>not </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>equal “should”. Take a poll of students who favor doing it because we can, and those who are in favor of questioning first IF we SHOULD.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p>11. <span><span><span><span><span><span>Assignment: Students write a one page (single-spaced) or two page (double-spaced) essay. They will articulate their position (with respect to the genetic condition they researched), reflecting on the choices faced by the parents of a fetus with that specific genetic condition.  What should they do and why? Would your answer change if it were your parents and if they were making the decision about your little brother or sister? Why would your answer change? Make sure to include vocabulary and concepts used in the two lessons as evidence for your answer.                                     </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>Rubric for Essay link: </span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Y9zQl1TThdNczqm-Ondn0c1o4D_j6-oqRSiLbQSXbMY/edit"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Y9zQl1TThdNczqm-Ondn0c1o4D_j6-oqRSiLbQSXbMY/edit</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Embedded assessments are located:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Lesson One, step 5.  After watching the short video, “What is Gene Editing and How Does It Work?”, students will be polled.  The questions and possible answers based on the video are listed below as well as in step 5 of Lesson One:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Poll students. What were some of the benefits indicated in the video? (possible answers: cure a disease, potential for fixing gene mutations that predispose people to certain cancers, enable new therapies for HIV, edit genes that cause hereditary diseases; in the plant world, make crops more nutritious, disease resistant, and able to grow in difficult conditions; in the animal world, can help them resist diseases, like preventing mosquitoes from carrying malaria)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Poll students. What are some of the downsides the video identified of gene editing? (possible answers: editing in human embryos for characteristics that have no bearing on health like eye color, like designer babies; potential to affect not only person, but their descendants; designer pets; more virulent microbial diseases)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Poll students. What are some ethical and societal concerns to consider that the video included? (possible answers: debate on regulating its use, regulating it, avoid negative use)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Lesson One, step 7.  At the end of the lesson, a knowledge check will be done to confirm whether or not the lesson plan met the learning objectives.  The learning objectives from lesson one are repeated here (as well as in step 2 of Lesson One):</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe the Catholic Social Teaching on the Dignity of the Human Person</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Define the term eugenics</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Explain how the CRISPR method of gene therapy works to target and modify genetic material</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluate the difference between genetic therapy and genetic enhancement</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>The knowledge check for these learning objectives will be done by requesting volunteers to answer questions posed below and then asking if anyone wants to add to the answers volunteers gave.  Then, the students will be polled about their agreement with the answers and the number will be placed on the board to assess whether or not the information from the lesson met the learning objectives and was clear enough to be comprehended.  The poll is listed below as well as in step 7 of Lesson One above:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to describe Catholic Social Teaching on the Dignity of the Human Person while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to define eugenics while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to explain how the CRISPR technology works while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to differentiate between genetic therapy and genetic enhancement while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Lesson Two, step 5.  As groups are working on their research, check in with groups to review their work, gauging their depth of thought and comprehension. From step 3, they have been broken up into smaller groups to research a medical condition or disease, its symptoms, and how the condition is transmitted (by either anomaly, defective/problematic gene or DNA sequence, inheritance pattern).</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Lesson Two, step 10.  At the end of the lesson, a knowledge check will be done to confirm whether or not the lesson plan met the learning objectives.  The learning objectives from lesson one are repeated here (as well as in step 2 of Lesson Two):</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe a medical condition or disease, its symptoms, and how it is transmitted</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluate how the theory/practice of eugenics violates the dignity of the human person</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analyze the moral, social, and economical consequences of genetic therapy/enhancement for a particular condition or disease</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Knowledge check based on learning objectives with combination of volunteers defining, polling, and sharing opinions and discussing.</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask for a volunteer to describe how the theory/practice of eugenics violates the dignity of the human person while I write that on the whiteboard. Ask if anyone would add to the description. Take a poll of how many students agree with the volunteer’s description (and addition or modification) and put that number on the whiteboard.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Ask students to share their opinion on the necessity for (take poll on how many think it’s necessary and write that number of students on the board). Then, ask students to share their opinion of the value of ethical considerations or administration over scientific exploration and experimentation while I write them on the whiteboard.  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Have students share their thoughts on the difference between the concepts of the secular bioethic technology imperative (because science is able to do it, science should do it) and the more religious bioethical imperative of considering just because science is able to do it, should we do it?  “Can” does not equal “should”. Take a poll of students who favor doing it because we can, and those who are in favor of questioning first IF we SHOULD.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>SUMMATIVE ASSESSMENTS:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><strong>Slideshow groups create based on research of assigned medical condition.  Rubric for Slideshow link: </strong></li> </ul> <p><a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/11o_pUIVVvwFzLpGrec8hVovN9XsGmw5evLYPVhk-A-o/edit"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://docs.google.com/document/d/11o_pUIVVvwFzLpGrec8hVovN9XsGmw5evLYPVhk-A-o/edit</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a></p> <ul> <li><strong>Essay students will complete at the end of the two lessons.</strong>  </li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Students write a one page (single-spaced) or two page (double-spaced) essay. They will articulate their position (with respect to the genetic condition they researched), reflecting on the choices faced by the parents of a fetus with that specific genetic condition.  What should they do and why? Would your answer change if it were your parents and if they were making the decision about your little brother or sister? Why would your answer change? Make sure to include vocabulary and concepts used in the two lessons as evidence for your answer. </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Rubric for field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Link to NGSS website: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><a href="https://www.nextgenscience.org/search-standards"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>https://www.nextgenscience.org/search-standards</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Next Generation Science Standards (NGSS):</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Understandings About the Nature of Science (High School)</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Scientific Knowledge is Open to Revision in Light of New Evidence</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Most scientific knowledge is quite durable but is, in principle, subject to change based on new evidence and/or reinterpretation of existing evidence.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Scientific argumentation is a mode of logical discourse used to clarify the strength of relationships between ideas and evidence that may result in revision of an explanation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science Models, Laws, Mechanisms, and Theories Explain Natural Phenomena</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>A scientific theory is a substantiated explanation of some aspect of the natural world, based on a body of facts that has been repeatedly confirmed through observation and experiment,and the science community validates each theory before it is accepted. If new evidence is discovered that the theory does not accommodate, the theory is generally modified in light of this new evidence</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science Addresses Questions About the Natural and Material World</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Not all questions can be answered by science</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p><br /> <span><span><span><strong><span><span> Link to USCCB (United States Conference of Catholic Bishops) Doctrinal Framework Standards:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><a href="http://www.usccb.org/beliefs-and-teachings/how-we-teach/catechesis/upload/high-school-curriculum-framework-adaptation-of-preamble-2.pdf"><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>http://www.usccb.org/beliefs-and-teachings/how-we-teach/catechesis/upload/high-school-curriculum-framework-adaptation-of-preamble-2.pdf</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></a></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>USCCB Doctrinal Framework Standards: </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>II. Who is Jesus Christ?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>    D. Jesus Christ teaches us about ourselves</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>The human person is created in the image and likeness of God. This means we are endowed with special gifts.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>CCC 357  Being in the image of God the human individual possesses the dignity of a person, who is not just something, but someone.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>         1700 The dignity of the human person is rooted in his creation in the image and likeness of God</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>        </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1704  ...By free will, he is capable of directing himself toward his true good. He finds his perfection “in seeking and loving what is true and good”</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>        1706  By his reason, man recognizes the voice of God which urges him “to do what is good and avoid what is evil”...Living a moral life bears witness to the dignity of the person.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>                    1745  Freedom characterizes properly human acts.  It makes the human being responsible for acts of which he is the voluntary agent.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>III. The Mission of Jesus Christ (The Paschal Mystery)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>The Creation of the world and our first parents</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3. Human beings are the summit of creation, made in the image and likeness of God</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Human persons are a union of body and soul and possess inviolable dignity</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>CCC 364 human body shares in the dignity of “the image of God”</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>VI. Life in Jesus Christ</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>     B. God teaches us how to live this new life</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Natural Moral Law</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>b. Basis for human rights and duties</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>CCC 1954 ...The natural law expresses the original moral sense which enables man to discern by reason the good and the evil,...</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>         1956 The natural law...expresses the dignity of the person and determines the basis for his fundamental rights and duties...</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Revelation</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>The Ten Commandments, as the privileged expression of the natural law...</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>5. You shall not kill</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>    CCC 2319 Every human life, from the moment of conception until death, is sacred because the human person has been willed for its own sake in the image and likeness of the living and holy God</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>             2320 The murder of a human being is gravely contrary to the dignity of the person and the holiness of the Creator</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>             2323 Because it should be treated as a person from conception, the embryo must be defended in its integrity, cared for, and healed like every other human being</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span> </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>                 c. The Church as teacher of moral principles</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>                      3. Church teaching forms one’s conscience for moral decision making</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>                      CCC 1776 deep within conscience, most secret core and his sanctuary    God’s voice echoes in his depths</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>                                       1778, 1796 Conscience - recognize moral quality of a concrete act</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>                                       1780 Dignity of human person implies and requires uprightness of moral conscience</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>                                        1781 Conscience enables one to assume responsibility for the acts performed</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Protocol Numbers (CCC):</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1926 common good must promote dignity of human person</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1945 equality is based on dignity and rights</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1947 dignity requires efforts to reduce How does the theory/practice of eugenics violate the dignity of the human person?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. What are the consequences of gene therapy being applied to conditions conditions such as Down Syndrome, blindness, deafness, and Autism Spectrum Disorder?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Should the concept of equitable care (availability of care to all persons at all economic levels) apply to medical technology such as CRISPR?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. To what extent are ethical considerations important when experimenting with gene therapy?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from
